Class representing an image (up to 4 dimensions wide), each pixel being of type {\ttfamily T}.

\subsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$typename T$>$ struct cimg\_\-library::CImg$<$ T $>$}

Class representing an image (up to 4 dimensions wide), each pixel being of type {\ttfamily T}. This is the main class of the CImg Library. It declares and constructs an image, allows access to its pixel values, and is able to perform various image operations.

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Image representation}

\end{DoxyParagraph}
A CImg image is defined as an instance of the container \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg}$<${\ttfamily T$>$}, which contains a regular grid of pixels, each pixel value being of type {\ttfamily T}. The image grid can have up to 4 dimensions : width, height, depth and number of channels. Usually, the three first dimensions are used to describe spatial coordinates {\ttfamily (x,y,z)}, while the number of channels is rather used as a vector-\/valued dimension (it may describe the R,G,B color channels for instance). If you need a fifth dimension, you can use image lists \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImgList}{CImgList}$<${\ttfamily T$>$} rather than simple images \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg}$<${\ttfamily T$>$}.

Thus, the \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg}$<${\ttfamily T$>$} class is able to represent volumetric images of vector-\/valued pixels, as well as images with less dimensions (1d scalar signal, 2d color images, ...). Most member functions of the class \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg}$<${\ttfamily T$>$} are designed to handle this maximum case of (3+1) dimensions.

Concerning the pixel value type {\ttfamily T} : fully supported template types are the basic C++ types : {\ttfamily unsigned char, char, short, unsigned int, int, unsigned long, long, float, double, ... }. Typically, fast image display can be done using {\ttfamily CImg$<$unsigned char$>$} images, while complex image processing algorithms may be rather coded using {\ttfamily CImg$<$float$>$} or {\ttfamily CImg$<$double$>$} images that have floating-\/point pixel values. The default value for the template T is {\ttfamily float}. Using your own template types may be possible. However, you will certainly have to define the complete set of arithmetic and logical operators for your class.

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Image structure}

\end{DoxyParagraph}
The \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg}$<${\ttfamily T$>$} structure contains {\itshape six\/} fields :
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a369399896761e31ae71db57fdd0ba431}{width} defines the number of {\itshape columns\/} of the image (size along the X-\/axis).
\item \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ae26bcfe2f33f5873dbdfb6948cf1f59f}{height} defines the number of {\itshape rows\/} of the image (size along the Y-\/axis).
\item \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3275d1392d01b26af1c8cd52b0d10745}{depth} defines the number of {\itshape slices\/} of the image (size along the Z-\/axis).
\item \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum} defines the number of {\itshape channels\/} of the image (size along the C-\/axis).
\item \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a1699472936b80a88d3fc8096975d21b2}{data} defines a {\itshape pointer\/} to the {\itshape pixel\/} {\itshape data\/} (of type {\ttfamily T}).
\item \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a89c9d2adf59c941c548b2dbb85d9224d}{is\_\-shared} is a boolean that tells if the memory buffer \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a1699472936b80a88d3fc8096975d21b2}{data} is shared with another image.
\end{DoxyItemize}

You can access these fields publicly although it is recommended to use the dedicated functions \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a369399896761e31ae71db57fdd0ba431}{width()}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ae26bcfe2f33f5873dbdfb6948cf1f59f}{height()}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3275d1392d01b26af1c8cd52b0d10745}{depth()}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum()} and ptr() to do so. Image dimensions are not limited to a specific range (as long as you got enough available memory). A value of {\itshape 1\/} usually means that the corresponding dimension is {\itshape flat\/}. If one of the dimensions is {\itshape 0\/}, or if the data pointer is null, the image is considered as {\itshape empty\/}. Empty images should not contain any pixel data and thus, will not be processed by \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg} member functions (a CImgInstanceException will be thrown instead). Pixel data are stored in memory, in a non interlaced mode (See cimg\_\-storage).

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Image declaration and construction}

\end{DoxyParagraph}
Declaring an image can be done by using one of the several available constructors. Here is a list of the most used :


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Construct images from arbitrary dimensions :
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg$<$char$>$} img;} declares an empty image.
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$unsigned char$>$ img(128,128);} declares a 128x128 greyscale image with {\ttfamily unsigned} {\ttfamily char} pixel values.
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$double$>$ img(3,3);} declares a 3x3 matrix with {\ttfamily double} coefficients.
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$unsigned char$>$ img(256,256,1,3);} declares a 256x256x1x3 (color) image (colors are stored as an image with three channels).
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$double$>$ img(128,128,128);} declares a 128x128x128 volumetric and greyscale image (with {\ttfamily double} pixel values).
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$$>$ img(128,128,128,3);} declares a 128x128x128 volumetric color image (with {\ttfamily float} pixels, which is the default value of the template parameter {\ttfamily T}).
\item {\bfseries Note} : images pixels are {\bfseries not automatically initialized to 0}. You may use the function \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a494a1e1424510af07e705dfe9b5f78bd}{fill()} to do it, or use the specific constructor taking 5 parameters like this : {\ttfamily CImg$<$$>$ img(128,128,128,3,0);} declares a 128x128x128 volumetric color image with all pixel values to 0.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Construct images from filenames :
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$unsigned char$>$ img(\char`\"{}image.jpg\char`\"{});} reads a JPEG color image from the file \char`\"{}image.jpg\char`\"{}.
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$float$>$ img(\char`\"{}analyze.hdr\char`\"{});} reads a volumetric image (ANALYZE7.5 format) from the file \char`\"{}analyze.hdr\char`\"{}.
\item {\bfseries Note} : You need to install \href{http://www.imagemagick.org}{\tt ImageMagick} to be able to read common compressed image formats (JPG,PNG, ...) (See cimg\_\-files\_\-io).
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Construct images from C-\/style arrays :
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$int$>$ img(data\_\-buffer,256,256);} constructs a 256x256 greyscale image from a {\ttfamily int$\ast$} buffer {\ttfamily data\_\-buffer} (of size 256x256=65536).
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$unsigned char$>$ img(data\_\-buffer,256,256,1,3,false);} constructs a 256x256 color image from a {\ttfamily unsigned} {\ttfamily char$\ast$} buffer {\ttfamily data\_\-buffer} (where R,G,B channels follow each others).
\item {\ttfamily CImg$<$unsigned char$>$ img(data\_\-buffer,256,256,1,3,true);} constructs a 256x256 color image from a {\ttfamily unsigned} {\ttfamily char$\ast$} buffer {\ttfamily data\_\-buffer} (where R,G,B channels are multiplexed).
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyItemize}

The complete list of constructors can be found \href{#constructors}{\tt here}.

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Most useful functions}

\end{DoxyParagraph}
The \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg}$<${\ttfamily T$>$} class contains a lot of functions that operates on images. Some of the most useful are :


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_accb8526e4303186fb6246ac1301fdf66}{operator()()} : allows to access or write pixel values.
\item \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_aea0592215c6068e617a975a1fe5b7b7b}{display()} : displays the image in a new window. 
\end{DoxyItemize}

Destructor. 

The destructor destroys the instance image. \begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Destructing an empty or shared image does nothing.
\item Otherwise, all memory used to store the pixel data of the instance image is freed.
\item When destroying a non-\/shared image, be sure that every shared instances of the same image are also destroyed to avoid further access to desallocated memory buffers. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a8a31842596268c9fc95810890607762f}{

Default constructor. 

The default constructor creates an empty instance image. \begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item An empty image does not contain any data and has all of its dimensions \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a369399896761e31ae71db57fdd0ba431}{width}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ae26bcfe2f33f5873dbdfb6948cf1f59f}{height}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3275d1392d01b26af1c8cd52b0d10745}{depth}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum} set to 0 as well as its pointer to the pixel buffer \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a1699472936b80a88d3fc8096975d21b2}{data}.
\item An empty image is non-\/shared. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}

Constructs a new image with given size ({\ttfamily dx},{\ttfamily dy},{\ttfamily dz},{\ttfamily dc}). 

This constructors create an instance image of size ({\ttfamily dx},{\ttfamily dy},{\ttfamily dz},{\ttfamily dc}) with pixels of type {\ttfamily T}. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em dx}]Desired size along the X-\/axis, i.e. the \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a369399896761e31ae71db57fdd0ba431}{width} of the image. \item[{\em dy}]Desired size along the Y-\/axis, i.e. the \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ae26bcfe2f33f5873dbdfb6948cf1f59f}{height} of the image. \item[{\em dz}]Desired size along the Z-\/axis, i.e. the \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3275d1392d01b26af1c8cd52b0d10745}{depth} of the image. \item[{\em dc}]Desired size along the C-\/axis, i.e. the number of image channels \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum}. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If one of the input dimension {\ttfamily dx},{\ttfamily dy},{\ttfamily dz} or {\ttfamily dc} is set to 0, the created image is empty and all has its dimensions set to 0. No memory for pixel data is then allocated.
\item This constructor creates only non-\/shared images.
\item Image pixels allocated by this constructor are {\bfseries not} {\bfseries initialized}. Use the constructor \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a456dc7452f9e0a0c820c469bb7ad2e2c}{CImg(const unsigned int,const unsigned int,const unsigned int,const unsigned int,const T)} to get an image of desired size with pixels set to a particular value. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}

Construct an image from an image file. 

This constructor creates an instance image by reading it from a file.

\item Recognized image formats depend on the tools installed on your system or the external libraries you use to link your code with. More informations on this topic can be found in cimg\_\-files\_\-io.
\item If the filename is not found, a CImgIOException is thrown by this constructor. 
\end{DoxyItemize}

\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const {\bf CImg}$<$ t $>$ \&}]{ img}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a8479cd0cf615e3131efcabac1e3ff004}


Default copy constructor. 

The default copy constructor creates a new instance image having same dimensions (\hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a369399896761e31ae71db57fdd0ba431}{width}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ae26bcfe2f33f5873dbdfb6948cf1f59f}{height}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3275d1392d01b26af1c8cd52b0d10745}{depth}, \_\-spectrum) and same pixel values as the input image {\ttfamily img}. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em img}]The input image to copy. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If the input image {\ttfamily img} is non-\/shared or have a different template type {\ttfamily t} != {\ttfamily T}, the default copy constructor allocates a new pixel buffer and copy the pixel data of {\ttfamily img} into it. In this case, the pointers \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a1699472936b80a88d3fc8096975d21b2}{data} to the pixel buffers of the two images are different and the resulting instance image is non-\/shared.
\item If the input image {\ttfamily img} is shared and has the same template type {\ttfamily t} == {\ttfamily T}, the default copy constructor does not allocate a new pixel buffer and the resulting instance image shares its pixel buffer with the input image {\ttfamily img}, which means that modifying pixels of {\ttfamily img} also modifies the created instance image.
\item Copying an image having a different template type {\ttfamily t} != {\ttfamily T} performs a crude static cast conversion of each pixel value from type {\ttfamily t} to type {\ttfamily T}.
\item Copying an image having the same template type {\ttfamily t} == {\ttfamily T} is significantly faster. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a8dfaf8ddcc86f17442f8eeb3102d0662}{
\index{cimg\_\-library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}!CImg@{CImg}}
\index{CImg@{CImg}!cimg_library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}}
\subsubsection[{CImg}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf CImg} (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const {\bf CImg}$<$ t $>$ \&}]{ img, }
\item[{const bool}]{ shared}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a8dfaf8ddcc86f17442f8eeb3102d0662}


Advanced copy constructor. 

The advanced copy constructor -\/ as the default constructor \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a8479cd0cf615e3131efcabac1e3ff004}{CImg(const CImg$<$ t $>$\&)} -\/ creates a new instance image having same dimensions \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a369399896761e31ae71db57fdd0ba431}{width}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ae26bcfe2f33f5873dbdfb6948cf1f59f}{height}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3275d1392d01b26af1c8cd52b0d10745}{depth}, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum} and same pixel values as the input image {\ttfamily img}. But it also decides if the created instance image shares its memory with the input image {\ttfamily img} (if the input parameter {\ttfamily shared} is set to {\ttfamily true}) or not (if the input parameter {\ttfamily shared} is set to {\ttfamily false}). 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em img}]The input image to copy. \item[{\em shared}]Boolean flag that decides if the copy is shared on non-\/shared. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item It is not possible to create a shared copy if the input image {\ttfamily img} is empty or has a different pixel type {\ttfamily t} != {\ttfamily T}.
\item If a non-\/shared copy of the input image {\ttfamily img} is created, a new memory buffer is allocated for pixel data.
\item If a shared copy of the input image {\ttfamily img} is created, no extra memory is allocated and the pixel buffer of the instance image is the same as the one used by the input image {\ttfamily img}. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a65018fb0cbdbd9e8d1404321cd69bfe5}


In-\/place version of the default constructor/destructor. 

This function replaces the instance image by an empty image. \begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Memory used by the previous content of the instance image is freed if necessary.
\item If the instance image was initially shared, it is replaced by a (non-\/shared) empty image.
\item This function is useful to free memory used by an image that is not of use, but which has been created in the current code scope (i.e. not destroyed yet). 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_aa04f124beb85fd91a13d3abc4fc83cb4}{

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_aa04f124beb85fd91a13d3abc4fc83cb4}


In-\/place version of the previous constructor. 

This function replaces the instance image by a new image of size ({\ttfamily dx},{\ttfamily dy},{\ttfamily dz},{\ttfamily dc}) with pixels of type {\ttfamily T}. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em dx}]Desired size along the X-\/axis, i.e. the \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a369399896761e31ae71db57fdd0ba431}{width} of the image. \item[{\em dy}]Desired size along the Y-\/axis, i.e. the \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ae26bcfe2f33f5873dbdfb6948cf1f59f}{height} of the image. \item[{\em dz}]Desired size along the Z-\/axis, i.e. the \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3275d1392d01b26af1c8cd52b0d10745}{depth} of the image. \item[{\em dc}]Desired size along the C-\/axis, i.e. the number of image channels {\ttfamily \_\-spectrum}.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If one of the input dimension {\ttfamily dx},{\ttfamily dy},{\ttfamily dz} or {\ttfamily dc} is set to 0, the instance image becomes empty and all has its dimensions set to 0. No memory for pixel data is then allocated.
\item Memory buffer used to store previous pixel values is freed if necessary.
\item If the instance image is shared, this constructor actually does nothing more than verifying that new and old image dimensions fit.
\item Image pixels allocated by this function are {\bfseries not} {\bfseries initialized}. Use the function \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_aa6265772f4f357317bca4c0cf677c462}{assign(const unsigned int,const unsigned int,const unsigned int,const unsigned int,const T)} to assign an image of desired size with pixels set to a particular value. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\end{DoxyParams}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_aa6265772f4f357317bca4c0cf677c462}{

In-\/place version of the previous constructor. 

This function replaces the instance image by a new image of size ({\ttfamily dx},{\ttfamily dy},{\ttfamily dz},{\ttfamily dc}) with pixels of type {\ttfamily T} and sets all pixel values of the instance image to {\ttfamily val}. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

In-\/place version of the previous constructor. 

This function replaces the instance image by the one that have been read from the given file. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em filename}]Filename of the image file.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The image format is deduced from the filename only by looking for the filename extension i.e. without analyzing the file itself.
\item Recognized image formats depend on the tools installed on your system or the external libraries you use to link your code with. More informations on this topic can be found in cimg\_\-files\_\-io.
\item If the filename is not found, a CImgIOException is thrown by this constructor. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\end{DoxyParams}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a0fb4ca12616b7a1a05a9b3cc62878df4}


In-\/place version of the default copy constructor. 

This function assigns a copy of the input image {\ttfamily img} to the current instance image. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em img}]The input image to copy. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If the instance image is non-\/shared, the content of the input image {\ttfamily img} is copied into a new buffer becoming the new pixel buffer of the instance image, while the old pixel buffer is freed if necessary.
\item If the instance image is shared, the content of the input image {\ttfamily img} is copied into the current (shared) pixel buffer of the instance image, modifying then the image referenced by the shared instance image. The instance image still remains shared. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a934bab7595fd98de5131d5d2394e4a81}{
\index{cimg\_\-library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}!assign@{assign}}
\index{assign@{assign}!cimg_library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}}

\begin{DoxyParamCaption}

\item[{const bool}]{ shared}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a934bab7595fd98de5131d5d2394e4a81}


In-\/place version of the advanced constructor. 

This function -\/ as the simpler function \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a0fb4ca12616b7a1a05a9b3cc62878df4}{assign(const CImg$<$ t $>$\&)} -\/ assigns a copy of the input image {\ttfamily img} to the current instance image. But it also decides if the copy is shared (if the input parameter {\ttfamily shared} is set to {\ttfamily true}) or non-\/shared (if the input parameter {\ttfamily shared} is set to {\ttfamily false}). 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em img}]The input image to copy. \item[{\em shared}]Boolean flag that decides if the copy is shared or non-\/shared. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item It is not possible to assign a shared copy if the input image {\ttfamily img} is empty or has a different pixel type {\ttfamily t} != {\ttfamily T}.
\item If a non-\/shared copy of the input image {\ttfamily img} is assigned, a new memory buffer is allocated for pixel data.
\item If a shared copy of the input image {\ttfamily img} is assigned, no extra memory is allocated and the pixel buffer of the instance image is the same as the one used by the input image {\ttfamily img}. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_accb8526e4303186fb6246ac1301fdf66}


Fast access to pixel value for reading or writing. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em x}]X-\/coordinate of the pixel. \item[{\em y}]Y-\/coordinate of the pixel. \item[{\em z}]Z-\/coordinate of the pixel. \item[{\em v}]C-\/coordinate of the pixel.\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If one image dimension is equal to 1, it can be omitted in the coordinate list (see example below).
\item If the macro {\ttfamily 'cimg\_\-verbosity'$>$=3}, boundary checking is performed and warning messages may appear (but function performances decrease).
\end{DoxyItemize}

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{example:}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       CImg<float> img(100,100,1,3,0);                       // Define a 100x100 
      color image with float-valued black pixels.
       const float valR = img(10,10,0,0);                    // Read the red comp
      onent at coordinates (10,10).
       const float valG = img(10,10,0,1);                    // Read the green co
      mponent at coordinates (10,10)
       const float valB = img(10,10,2);                      // Read the blue com
      ponent at coordinates (10,10) (Z-coordinate omitted here).
       const float avg = (valR + valG + valB)/3;             // Compute average p
      ixel value.
       img(10,10,0) = img(10,10,1) = img(10,10,2) = avg;     // Replace the pixel
       (10,10) by the average grey value.
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

Return a pointer to the pixel value located at ({\ttfamily x},{\ttfamily y},{\ttfamily z},{\ttfamily v}). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em x}]X-\/coordinate of the pixel. \item[{\em y}]Y-\/coordinate of the pixel. \item[{\em z}]Z-\/coordinate of the pixel. \item[{\em v}]C-\/coordinate of the pixel.\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item When called without parameters, \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a1699472936b80a88d3fc8096975d21b2}{data()} returns a pointer to the begining of the pixel buffer.
\item If the macro {\ttfamily 'cimg\_\-verbosity'$>$=3}, boundary checking is performed and warning messages may appear if given coordinates are outside the image range (but function performances decrease).
\end{DoxyItemize}

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{example:}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       CImg<float> img(100,100,1,1,0);   // Define a 100x100 greyscale image with
       float-valued pixels.
       float *ptr = data(10,10);         // Get a pointer to the pixel located at
       (10,10).
       float val = *ptr;                 // Get the pixel value.
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a392f71cadb214ede4a723315f44f371c}{
\index{cimg\_\-library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}!variance@{variance}}
\index{variance@{variance}!cimg_library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}}
\subsubsection[{variance}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}Tdouble variance (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const unsigned int}]{ variance\_\-method = {\ttfamily 1}}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a392f71cadb214ede4a723315f44f371c}


Return the variance of the image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em variance\_\-method}]Determines how to calculate the variance \begin{TabularC}{2}
\hline
0 &Second moment: $ v = 1/N \sum\limits_{k=1}^{N} (x_k - \bar x)^2 = 1/N \left( \sum\limits_{k=1}^N x_k^2 - \left( \sum\limits_{k=1}^N x_k \right)^2 / N \right) $ with $ \bar x = 1/N \sum\limits_{k=1}^N x_k $ \\\cline{1-2}
1 &Best unbiased estimator: $ v = \frac{1}{N-1} \sum\limits_{k=1}^{N} (x_k - \bar x)^2 $ \\\cline{1-2}
2 &Least median of squares \\\cline{1-2}
3 &Least trimmed of squares \\\cline{1-2}
\end{TabularC}
\end{DoxyParams}

\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acaf16c667ccfe861ba7c565537f67a1a}{
\index{cimg\_\-library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}!noise@{noise}}
\index{noise@{noise}!cimg_library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}}
\subsubsection[{noise}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf CImg}$<$T$>$\& noise (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const double}]{ sigma, }
\item[{const unsigned int}]{ noise\_\-type = {\ttfamily 0}}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acaf16c667ccfe861ba7c565537f67a1a}


Add random noise to the values of the instance image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em sigma}]Amplitude of the random additive noise. If {\ttfamily sigma$<$0}, it stands for a percentage of the global value range. \item[{\em noise\_\-type}]Type of additive noise (can be {\ttfamily 0=gaussian}, {\ttfamily 1=uniform}, {\ttfamily 2=Salt} and Pepper, {\ttfamily 3=Poisson} or {\ttfamily 4=Rician}). \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A reference to the modified instance image. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item For Poisson noise ({\ttfamily noise\_\-type=3}), parameter {\ttfamily sigma} is ignored, as Poisson noise only depends on the image value itself.
\item Function {\ttfamily CImg$<$T$>$::get\_\-noise()} is also defined. It returns a non-\/shared modified copy of the instance image. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Sample code :}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       const CImg<float> img("reference.jpg"), res = img.get_noise(40);
       (img,res.normalize(0,255)).display();
\end{DoxyCode}
  
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3513f6abbbfb7c9f025f9981ae52de90}{
\index{cimg\_\-library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}!histogram@{histogram}}
\index{histogram@{histogram}!cimg_library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}}
\subsubsection[{histogram}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf CImg}$<$T$>$\& histogram (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const unsigned int}]{ nb\_\-levels, }
\item[{const T}]{ value\_\-min = {\ttfamily (T)0}, }
\item[{const T}]{ value\_\-max = {\ttfamily (T)0}}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3513f6abbbfb7c9f025f9981ae52de90}


Compute the histogram of the instance image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em nb\_\-levels}]Number of desired histogram levels. \item[{\em value\_\-min}]Minimum pixel value considered for the histogram computation. All pixel values lower than {\ttfamily value\_\-min} will not be counted. \item[{\em value\_\-max}]Maximum pixel value considered for the histogram computation. All pixel values higher than {\ttfamily value\_\-max} will not be counted. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Instance image is replaced by its histogram, defined as a {\ttfamily CImg$<$T$>$(nb\_\-levels)} image. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The histogram H of an image I is the 1d function where H(x) counts the number of occurences of the value x in the image I.
\item If {\ttfamily value\_\-min==value\_\-max==0} (default behavior), the function first estimates the whole range of pixel values then uses it to compute the histogram.
\item The resulting histogram is always defined in 1d. Histograms of multi-\/valued images are not multi-\/dimensional.
\item Function {\ttfamily CImg$<$T$>$::get\_\-histogram()} is also defined. It returns a non-\/shared modified copy of the instance image. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Sample code :}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       const CImg<float> img = CImg<float>("reference.jpg").histogram(256);
       img.display_graph(0,3);
\end{DoxyCode}
  
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a62191853dd65b6f5cbc43e7a63a74832}{

Compute the histogram-\/equalized version of the instance image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em nb\_\-levels}]Number of histogram levels used for the equalization. \item[{\em value\_\-min}]Minimum pixel value considered for the histogram computation. All pixel values lower than {\ttfamily value\_\-min} will not be counted. \item[{\em value\_\-max}]Maximum pixel value considered for the histogram computation. All pixel values higher than {\ttfamily value\_\-max} will not be counted. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A reference to the modified instance image.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If {\ttfamily value\_\-min==value\_\-max==0} (default behavior), the function first estimates the whole range of pixel values then uses it to equalize the histogram.
\item Function {\ttfamily CImg$<$T$>$::get\_\-equalize()} is also defined. It returns a non-\/shared modified copy of the instance image.

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a06115492b8d5f2e6af399c84eb07c1ee}


Index multi-\/valued pixels of the instance image, regarding to a predefined palette. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em palette}]Multi-\/valued palette used as the basis for multi-\/valued pixel indexing. \item[{\em dithering}]Tells if Floyd-\/Steinberg dithering is activated or not. \item[{\em map\_\-indexes}]Tell if the values of the resulting image are the palette indices or the palette vectors. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A reference to the modified instance image. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily img.index(palette,dithering,1)} is equivalent to {\ttfamily img.index(palette,dithering,0).map(palette)}.
\item Function {\ttfamily CImg$<$T$>$::get\_\-index()} is also defined. It returns a non-\/shared modified copy of the instance image. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Sample code :}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       const CImg<float> img("reference.jpg"), palette(3,1,1,3, 0,128,255, 0,128,
      255, 0,128,255);
       const CImg<float> res = img.get_index(palette,true,true);
       (img,res).display();
\end{DoxyCode}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a1fe154cd43b8bf4b95fad6c8e2b853df}


Map predefined palette on the scalar (indexed) instance image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em palette}]Multi-\/valued palette used for mapping the indexes. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A reference to the modified instance image. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Function {\ttfamily CImg$<$T$>$::get\_\-map()} is also defined. It returns a non-\/shared modified copy of the instance image. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Sample code :}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       const CImg<float> img("reference.jpg"),
                         palette1(3,1,1,3, 0,128,255, 0,128,255, 0,128,255),
                         palette2(3,1,1,3, 255,0,0, 0,255,0, 0,0,255),
                         res = img.get_index(palette1,false).map(palette2);
       (img,res).display();
\end{DoxyCode}
  
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a2fa6df9e3b47fc86c59851cadaf6e3e6}


Resize an image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em size\_\-x}]Number of columns (new size along the X-\/axis). \item[{\em size\_\-y}]Number of rows (new size along the Y-\/axis). \item[{\em size\_\-z}]Number of slices (new size along the Z-\/axis). \item[{\em size\_\-c}]Number of vector-\/channels (new size along the C-\/axis). \item[{\em interpolation\_\-type}]Method of interpolation :
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item -\/1 = no interpolation : raw memory resizing.
\item 0 = no interpolation : additional space is filled according to {\ttfamily border\_\-condition}.
\item 1 = nearest-\/neighbor interpolation.
\item 2 = moving average interpolation.
\item 3 = linear interpolation.
\item 4 = grid interpolation.
\item 5 = bicubic interpolation.
\item 6 = lanczos interpolation. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\item[{\em border\_\-conditions}]Border condition type. \item[{\em centering\_\-x}]Set centering type (only if {\ttfamily interpolation\_\-type=0}). \item[{\em centering\_\-y}]Set centering type (only if {\ttfamily interpolation\_\-type=0}). \item[{\em centering\_\-z}]Set centering type (only if {\ttfamily interpolation\_\-type=0}). \item[{\em centering\_\-c}]Set centering type (only if {\ttfamily interpolation\_\-type=0}). \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
If pd\mbox{[}x,y,z,v\mbox{]}$<$0, it corresponds to a percentage of the original size (the default value is -\/100). 
\end{DoxyNote}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_aa2fa295816582cb2e62d530c54533055}{

Compute the correlation of the instance image by a mask. 

The correlation of the instance image {\ttfamily $\ast$this} by the mask {\ttfamily mask} is defined to be :

res(x,y,z) = sum\_\-\{i,j,k\} ($\ast$this)(x+i,y+j,z+k)$\ast$mask(i,j,k)


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em mask}]= the correlation kernel. \item[{\em border\_\-conditions}]= the border condition type (0=zero, 1=dirichlet) \item[{\em is\_\-normalized}]= enable local normalization. \end{DoxyParams}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acf2efb8768c7a62d89c489ffcf9acf6e}{

\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acf2efb8768c7a62d89c489ffcf9acf6e}


Compute the convolution of the image by a mask. 

The result {\ttfamily res} of the convolution of an image {\ttfamily img} by a mask {\ttfamily mask} is defined to be :

res(x,y,z) = sum\_\-\{i,j,k\} img(x-\/i,y-\/j,z-\/k)$\ast$mask(i,j,k)


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em mask}]= the correlation kernel. \item[{\em border\_\-conditions}]= the border condition type (0=zero, 1=dirichlet) \item[{\em is\_\-normalized}]= enable local normalization. \end{DoxyParams}

Blur the image anisotropically following a field of diffusion tensors. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em G}]= Field of square roots of diffusion tensors/vectors used to drive the smoothing. \item[{\em amplitude}]= amplitude of the smoothing. \item[{\em dl}]= spatial discretization. \item[{\em da}]= angular discretization. \item[{\em gauss\_\-prec}]= precision of the gaussian function. \item[{\em interpolation}]Used interpolation scheme (0 = nearest-\/neighbor, 1 = linear, 2 = Runge-\/Kutta) \item[{\em fast\_\-approx}]= Tell to use the fast approximation or not. \end{DoxyParams}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a42321139d023b6603e197799d16b6ead}{
\index{cimg\_\-library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}!blur\_\-bilateral@{blur\_\-bilateral}}

\begin{DoxyParamCaption}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a42321139d023b6603e197799d16b6ead}


Blur an image using the bilateral filter. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em sigma\_\-x}]Amount of blur along the X-\/axis. \item[{\em sigma\_\-y}]Amount of blur along the Y-\/axis. \item[{\em sigma\_\-z}]Amount of blur along the Z-\/axis. \item[{\em sigma\_\-r}]Amount of blur along the range axis. \item[{\em bgrid\_\-x}]Size of the bilateral grid along the X-\/axis. \item[{\em bgrid\_\-y}]Size of the bilateral grid along the Y-\/axis. \item[{\em bgrid\_\-z}]Size of the bilateral grid along the Z-\/axis. \item[{\em bgrid\_\-r}]Size of the bilateral grid along the range axis. \item[{\em interpolation\_\-type}]Use interpolation for image slicing. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This algorithm uses the optimisation technique proposed by S. Paris and F. Durand, in ECCV'2006 (extended for 3d volumetric images). 
\end{DoxyNote}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3e5b54c0b862cbf6e9f14e832984c4d7}{
\index{cimg\_\-library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}!get\_\-gradient@{get\_\-gradient}}

\begin{DoxyParamCaption}

\item[{const int}]{ scheme = {\ttfamily 3}}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a3e5b54c0b862cbf6e9f14e832984c4d7}


Compute the list of images, corresponding to the XY-\/gradients of an image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em scheme}]= Numerical scheme used for the gradient computation :
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item -\/1 = Backward finite differences
\item 0 = Centered finite differences
\item 1 = Forward finite differences
\item 2 = Using Sobel masks
\item 3 = Using rotation invariant masks
\item 4 = Using Deriche recusrsive filter. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\end{DoxyParams}

       CImg<unsigned char>().display_object3d("Sphere3d",points3d,faces3d);
\end{DoxyCode}
  
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ae24de98deb46f84769fd72c504ceedc2}


Create and return a 3d ellipsoid. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[\mbox{\tt[out]} {\em primitives}]The returned list of the 3d object primitives (template type {\itshape tf\/} should be at least {\itshape unsigned\/} {\itshape int\/}). \item[{\em tensor}]The tensor which gives the shape and size of the ellipsoid. \item[{\em subdivisions}]The number of recursive subdivisions from an initial stretched icosahedron. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The N vertices (xi,yi,zi) of the 3d object as a Nx3 CImg$<$float$>$ image (0$<$=i$<$=N-\/1). 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Sample code :}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       CImgList<unsigned int> faces3d;
       const CImg<float> tensor = CImg<float>::diagonal(10,7,3),
                         points3d = CImg<float>::ellipsoid3d(faces3d,tensor,4);
       CImg<unsigned char>().display_object3d("Ellipsoid3d",points3d,faces3d);
\end{DoxyCode}
  
\end{DoxyParagraph}

Draw a 2d colored point (pixel). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em x0}]X-\/coordinate of the point. \item[{\em y0}]Y-\/coordinate of the point. \item[{\em color}]Pointer to {\ttfamily \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum()}} consecutive values, defining the color values. \item[{\em opacity}]Drawing opacity (optional). \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Clipping is supported.
\item To set pixel values without clipping needs, you should use the faster \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_accb8526e4303186fb6246ac1301fdf66}{CImg::operator()()} function. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example:}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       CImg<unsigned char> img(100,100,1,3,0);
       const unsigned char color[] = { 255,128,64 };
       img.draw_point(50,50,color);
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a88ccbeac12af8b83cd17f9b72bbfe73b}


Draw a 2d colored line. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em x0}]X-\/coordinate of the starting line point. \item[{\em y0}]Y-\/coordinate of the starting line point. \item[{\em x1}]X-\/coordinate of the ending line point. \item[{\em y1}]Y-\/coordinate of the ending line point. \item[{\em color}]Pointer to {\ttfamily \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum()}} consecutive values of type {\ttfamily T}, defining the drawing color. \item[{\em opacity}]Drawing opacity (optional). \item[{\em pattern}]An integer whose bits describe the line pattern (optional). \item[{\em init\_\-hatch}]Flag telling if a reinitialization of the hash state must be done (optional). \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Clipping is supported.
\item Line routine uses Bresenham's algorithm.
\item Set {\ttfamily init\_\-hatch} = false to draw consecutive hatched segments without breaking the line pattern. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example:}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       CImg<unsigned char> img(100,100,1,3,0);
       const unsigned char color[] = { 255,128,64 };
        img.draw_line(40,40,80,70,color);
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

Draw a 2d textured line. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em x0}]X-\/coordinate of the starting line point. \item[{\em y0}]Y-\/coordinate of the starting line point. \item[{\em x1}]X-\/coordinate of the ending line point. \item[{\em y1}]Y-\/coordinate of the ending line point. \item[{\em texture}]Texture image defining the pixel colors. \item[{\em tx0}]X-\/coordinate of the starting texture point. \item[{\em ty0}]Y-\/coordinate of the starting texture point. \item[{\em tx1}]X-\/coordinate of the ending texture point. \item[{\em ty1}]Y-\/coordinate of the ending texture point. \item[{\em opacity}]Drawing opacity (optional). \item[{\em pattern}]An integer whose bits describe the line pattern (optional). \item[{\em init\_\-hatch}]Flag telling if the hash variable must be reinitialized (optional). \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Clipping is supported but not for texture coordinates.
\item Line routine uses the well known Bresenham's algorithm. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example:}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       CImg<unsigned char> img(100,100,1,3,0), texture("texture256x256.ppm");
       const unsigned char color[] = { 255,128,64 };
       img.draw_line(40,40,80,70,texture,0,0,255,255);
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_af42f741d0f579a78f9f58d0d6499bc53}


Draw a set of consecutive colored lines in the instance image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em points}]Coordinates of vertices, stored as a list of vectors. \item[{\em color}]Pointer to {\ttfamily \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum()}} consecutive values of type {\ttfamily T}, defining the drawing color. \item[{\em opacity}]Drawing opacity (optional). \item[{\em pattern}]An integer whose bits describe the line pattern (optional). \item[{\em init\_\-hatch}]If set to true, init hatch motif. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item This function uses several call to the single \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a88ccbeac12af8b83cd17f9b72bbfe73b}{CImg::draw\_\-line()} procedure, depending on the vectors size in {\ttfamily points}. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example:}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       CImg<unsigned char> img(100,100,1,3,0);
       const unsigned char color[] = { 255,128,64 };
       CImgList<int> points;
       points.insert(CImg<int>::vector(0,0)).
             .insert(CImg<int>::vector(70,10)).
             .insert(CImg<int>::vector(80,60)).
             .insert(CImg<int>::vector(10,90));
       img.draw_line(points,color);
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a2ff5e462fffb6048577ff02ac95431aa}


Draw a cubic spline curve in the instance image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em x0}]X-\/coordinate of the starting curve point \item[{\em y0}]Y-\/coordinate of the starting curve point \item[{\em u0}]X-\/coordinate of the starting velocity \item[{\em v0}]Y-\/coordinate of the starting velocity \item[{\em x1}]X-\/coordinate of the ending curve point \item[{\em y1}]Y-\/coordinate of the ending curve point \item[{\em u1}]X-\/coordinate of the ending velocity \item[{\em v1}]Y-\/coordinate of the ending velocity \item[{\em color}]Pointer to {\ttfamily \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum()}} consecutive values of type {\ttfamily T}, defining the drawing color. \item[{\em precision}]Curve drawing precision (optional). \item[{\em opacity}]Drawing opacity (optional). \item[{\em pattern}]An integer whose bits describe the line pattern (optional). \item[{\em init\_\-hatch}]If {\ttfamily true}, init hatch motif. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The curve is a 2d cubic Bezier spline, from the set of specified starting/ending points and corresponding velocity vectors.
\item The spline is drawn as a serie of connected segments. The {\ttfamily precision} parameter sets the average number of pixels in each drawn segment.
\item A cubic Bezier curve is sometimes defined by a set of 4 points \{ ({\ttfamily x0},{\ttfamily y0}), ({\ttfamily xa},{\ttfamily ya}), ({\ttfamily xb},{\ttfamily yb}), ({\ttfamily x1},{\ttfamily y1}) \} where ({\ttfamily x0},{\ttfamily y0}) is the starting point, ({\ttfamily x1},{\ttfamily y1}) is the ending point and ({\ttfamily xa},{\ttfamily ya}), ({\ttfamily xb},{\ttfamily yb}) are two {\itshape control\/} points. The starting and ending velocities ({\ttfamily u0},{\ttfamily v0}) and ({\ttfamily u1},{\ttfamily v1}) can be deduced easily from the control points as {\ttfamily u0} = ({\ttfamily xa} -\/ {\ttfamily x0}), {\ttfamily v0} = ({\ttfamily ya} -\/ {\ttfamily y0}), {\ttfamily u1} = ({\ttfamily x1} -\/ {\ttfamily xb}) and {\ttfamily v1} = ({\ttfamily y1} -\/ {\ttfamily yb}). 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example:}

\begin{DoxyCode}
       CImg<unsigned char> img(100,100,1,3,0);
       const unsigned char color[] = { 255,255,255 };
       img.draw_spline(30,30,0,100,90,40,0,-100,color);
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a111ec303273ffc87a1be739275957c92}{

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em x0}]= X-\/coordinate of the first corner in the instance image. \item[{\em y0}]= Y-\/coordinate of the first corner in the instance image. \item[{\em x1}]= X-\/coordinate of the second corner in the instance image. \item[{\em y1}]= Y-\/coordinate of the second corner in the instance image. \item[{\em x2}]= X-\/coordinate of the third corner in the instance image. \item[{\em y2}]= Y-\/coordinate of the third corner in the instance image. \item[{\em color}]= array of \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum()} values of type {\ttfamily T}, defining the global drawing color. \item[{\em brightness0}]= brightness of the first corner (in \mbox{[}0,2\mbox{]}). \item[{\em brightness1}]= brightness of the second corner (in \mbox{[}0,2\mbox{]}). \item[{\em brightness2}]= brightness of the third corner (in \mbox{[}0,2\mbox{]}). \item[{\em opacity}]= opacity of the drawing. \end{DoxyParams}

Draw a 2d textured triangle. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em x0}]= X-\/coordinate of the first corner in the instance image. \item[{\em y0}]= Y-\/coordinate of the first corner in the instance image. \item[{\em x1}]= X-\/coordinate of the second corner in the instance image. \item[{\em y1}]= Y-\/coordinate of the second corner in the instance image. \item[{\em x2}]= X-\/coordinate of the third corner in the instance image. \item[{\em y2}]= Y-\/coordinate of the third corner in the instance image. \item[{\em texture}]= texture image used to fill the triangle. \item[{\em tx0}]= X-\/coordinate of the first corner in the texture image. \item[{\em ty0}]= Y-\/coordinate of the first corner in the texture image. \item[{\em tx1}]= X-\/coordinate of the second corner in the texture image. \item[{\em ty1}]= Y-\/coordinate of the second corner in the texture image. \item[{\em tx2}]= X-\/coordinate of the third corner in the texture image. \item[{\em ty2}]= Y-\/coordinate of the third corner in the texture image. \item[{\em opacity}]= opacity of the drawing. \item[{\em brightness}]= brightness of the drawing (in \mbox{[}0,2\mbox{]}). \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
Clipping is supported, but texture coordinates do not support clipping. 
\end{DoxyNote}

Draw a sprite image in the instance image (masked version). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em sprite}]Sprite image. \item[{\em mask}]Mask image. \item[{\em x0}]X-\/coordinate of the sprite position in the instance image. \item[{\em y0}]Y-\/coordinate of the sprite position in the instance image. \item[{\em z0}]Z-\/coordinate of the sprite position in the instance image. \item[{\em c0}]C-\/coordinate of the sprite position in the instance image. \item[{\em mask\_\-valmax}]Maximum pixel value of the mask image {\ttfamily mask} (optional). \item[{\em opacity}]Drawing opacity. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Pixel values of {\ttfamily mask} set the opacity of the corresponding pixels in {\ttfamily sprite}.
\item Clipping is supported.
\item Dimensions along x,y and z of {\ttfamily sprite} and {\ttfamily mask} must be the same. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}

Draw a 1d graph on the instance image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em data}]Image containing the graph values I = f(x). \item[{\em color}]Array of \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_acd2ee207fa512e34b45ff548082f70ba}{spectrum()} values of type {\ttfamily T}, defining the drawing color. \item[{\em opacity}]Drawing opacity.\item[{\em plot\_\-type}]Define the type of the plot :
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 0 = No plot.
\item 1 = Plot using segments.
\item 2 = Plot using cubic splines.
\item 3 = Plot with bars. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\item[{\em vertex\_\-type}]Define the type of points :
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 0 = No points.
\item 1 = Point.
\item 2 = Straight cross.
\item 3 = Diagonal cross.
\item 4 = Filled circle.
\item 5 = Outlined circle.
\item 6 = Square.
\item 7 = Diamond. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\item[{\em ymin}]Lower bound of the y-\/range. \item[{\em ymax}]Upper bound of the y-\/range. \item[{\em pattern}]Drawing pattern. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item if {\ttfamily ymin==ymax==0}, the y-\/range is computed automatically from the input samples. 
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}

Draw a 3d object. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em X}]= X-\/coordinate of the 3d object position \item[{\em Y}]= Y-\/coordinate of the 3d object position \item[{\em Z}]= Z-\/coordinate of the 3d object position \item[{\em vertices}]= Image Nx3 describing 3d point coordinates \item[{\em primitives}]= List of P primitives \item[{\em colors}]= List of P color (or textures) \item[{\em opacities}]= Image or list of P opacities \item[{\em render\_\-type}]= Render type (0=Points, 1=Lines, 2=Faces (no light), 3=Faces (flat), 4=Faces(Gouraud) \item[{\em double\_\-sided}]= Tell if object faces have two sides or are oriented. \item[{\em focale}]= length of the focale (0 for parallel projection) \item[{\em lightx}]= X-\/coordinate of the light \item[{\em lighty}]= Y-\/coordinate of the light \item[{\em lightz}]= Z-\/coordinate of the light \item[{\em specular\_\-shine}]= Shininess of the object \end{DoxyParams}

Simple interface to select a shape from an image. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em selection}]Array of 6 values containing the selection result \item[{\em coords\_\-type}]Determine shape type to select (0=point, 1=vector, 2=rectangle, 3=circle) \item[{\em disp}]Display window used to make the selection \item[{\em XYZ}]Initial XYZ position (for volumetric images only) \item[{\em color}]Color of the shape selector. \end{DoxyParams}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a138dcc5db93d511d224d88405a0041ce}


Load an image from a file. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em filename}]is the name of the image file to load. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The extension of {\ttfamily filename} defines the file format. If no filename extension is provided, CImg$<$T$>$::get\_\-load() will try to load a .cimg file. 
\end{DoxyNote}
\hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ab943c007a92b463ec458b4be80e80460}{

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ab943c007a92b463ec458b4be80e80460}


Load an image from a TIFF file. 


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item libtiff support is enabled by defining the precompilation directive cimg\_\-use\_\-tif.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item When libtiff is enabled, 2D and 3D (multipage) several channel per pixel are supported for char,uchar,short,ushort,float and double pixel type.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If cimg\_\-use\_\-tif is not defined at compilation time the function uses CImg$<$T$>$\&\hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_a35a909fb3df4bd76be2facc8366861af}{load\_\-other(const char$\ast$)}.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Save the image as a file. 

The used file format is defined by the file extension in the filename {\ttfamily filename}. Parameter {\ttfamily number} can be used to add a 6-\/digit number to the filename before saving. \hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ad17e8b00c13b9724696b2bd3d2f7cf7b}{

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ad17e8b00c13b9724696b2bd3d2f7cf7b}


Save a file in TIFF format. 


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item libtiff support is enabled by defining the precompilation directive cimg\_\-use\_\-tif.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item When libtiff is enabled, 2D and 3D (multipage) several channel per pixel are supported for char,uchar,short,ushort,float and double pixel type.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If cimg\_\-use\_\-tif is not defined at compilation time the function uses CImg$<$T$>$\&save\_\-other(const char$\ast$).
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em compression}]1:None, 2:CCITTRLE, 3:CCITTFAX3, 4:CCITTFAX4, 5:LZW, 6:JPEG\end{DoxyParams}

\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_afdab21cdc4ef778bfaf4e123b28c9aa0}


Save the image using GraphicsMagick's gm. 

Function that saves the image for other file formats that are not natively handled by \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg}, using the tool 'gm' from the GraphicsMagick package.\par
 This is the case for all compressed image formats (GIF,PNG,JPG,TIF, ...). You need to install the GraphicsMagick package in order to get this function working properly (see \href{http://www.graphicsmagick.org}{\tt http://www.graphicsmagick.org} ). \hypertarget{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ab0ff4f35fc74d40fda4893b7e2fdbe7b}{
\index{cimg\_\-library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}!save\_\-imagemagick\_\-external@{save\_\-imagemagick\_\-external}}
\index{save\_\-imagemagick\_\-external@{save\_\-imagemagick\_\-external}!cimg_library::CImg@{cimg\_\-library::CImg}}
\subsubsection[{save\_\-imagemagick\_\-external}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}const {\bf CImg}$<$T$>$\& save\_\-imagemagick\_\-external (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const char $\ast$const }]{ filename, }
\item[{const unsigned int}]{ quality = {\ttfamily 100}}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}
\label{structcimg__library_1_1CImg_ab0ff4f35fc74d40fda4893b7e2fdbe7b}


Save the image using ImageMagick's convert. 

Function that saves the image for other file formats that are not natively handled by \hyperlink{structcimg__library_1_1CImg}{CImg}, using the tool 'convert' from the ImageMagick package.\par
 This is the case for all compressed image formats (GIF,PNG,JPG,TIF, ...). You need to install the ImageMagick package in order to get this function working properly (see \href{http://www.imagemagick.org}{\tt http://www.imagemagick.org} ).
